  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_264ff868-6843-44b8-aca4-8814e0f05669'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1735610137960695899">Listen, Little Man! is a great physician's quiet talk to each one of us, the average human being, the Little Man. Written in 1946 in answer to the gossip and defamation that plagued his remarkable career, it tells how Reich watched, at first naively, then with amazement, and finally with horror, at what the Little Man does to himself; how he suffers and rebels; how he este</span>
  <span id="freeText1735610137960695899" style="display:none">Listen, Little Man! is a great physician's quiet talk to each one of us, the average human being, the Little Man. Written in 1946 in answer to the gossip and defamation that plagued his remarkable career, it tells how Reich watched, at first naively, then with amazement, and finally with horror, at what the Little Man does to himself; how he suffers and rebels; how he esteems his enemies and murders his friends; how, wherever he gains power as a "representative of the people," he misuses this power and makes it crueler than the power it has supplanted.<br /><br />Reich has us to look honestly at ourselves and to assume responsibility for our lives and for the great untapped potential that lies in the depth of human nature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1735610137960695899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_840007536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ademption" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1045093-ademption"><img alt="Ademption" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264349089p2/1045093.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/840007536?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2014</a>

        <a title="Ademption" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ademption" href="/user/show/1045093-ademption">Ademption</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1045093-ademption?shelf=german-literature">german-literature</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer840007536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10935739333031320953">Looking for a sustained rant of 130ish pages? This may be your book. Wilhelm Reich was a noted psychoanalyst and Austrian MD, lauded in Sigmund Freud's inner circle for the concept of character armour, i.e. people closing up and dealing with only a slice of the incoming sense data about the world in order to protect themselves, becoming an expert in that slice, and sniping from within the protection of that narrow fetishization of the world.<br/><br/>Later on, he fell out of favour with Freud when he bega</span>
  <span id="freeText10935739333031320953" style="display:none">Looking for a sustained rant of 130ish pages? This may be your book. Wilhelm Reich was a noted psychoanalyst and Austrian MD, lauded in Sigmund Freud's inner circle for the concept of character armour, i.e. people closing up and dealing with only a slice of the incoming sense data about the world in order to protect themselves, becoming an expert in that slice, and sniping from within the protection of that narrow fetishization of the world.<br /><br />Later on, he fell out of favour with Freud when he began experimenting with what he called "orgone," or human life force, which could be ascertained like an aura under certain scientifical conditions in the dark. According to Reich, orgone is increased by doing what you love, meditating, encouraging others to be their best selves, and having copious amounts of sex.<br /><br />During and after WII, he was refused medical licences throughout Europe and the US, as he emigrated westward, because of his zany view that people should be getting off lots and not shy talking about it. Personally, Reich had lots of sex with many ladies he worked with in hospitals, labs, or clinics, whether staff or patients, which was found to be both ethically troubling and scintillating.<br /><br />He built orgone accumulators, which are essentially upright wooden boxes with a door and a bench inside, where a person sits, meditating on his or her life force and thereby accumulating more of it. The Beat poets, Sean Connery, J.D. Salinger, and Robert Anton Wilson had orgone accumulators. Some of these men probably sat inside them hoping to lay as much pipe as Reich. I find this rather funny, a psychoanalyst getting 1950s type-men to calmly meditate and self-reflect through the promise of more sex. <br /><br />Reich was as unashamed as a clinician talking about sex. In the 1940s and 50s. In America. This did not go well.<br /><br />Reich was probably gently mad in his old age. He milled around his Maine estate, building and selling orgone accumulators, working away on his cure for cancer that yielded results that only he could see, much like orgone, and building cloudbusters, i.e. gun-shaped turret-shells he claimed dissipated clouds. At one point, Albert Einstein experimented with both the accumulators and Reich's cancer cure and diplomatically stopped speaking with Reich, who either wanted confirmation or to argue someone into yielding confirmation.<br /><br />Eventually, someone found him weird enough to poke at, question his views enough to fuck up his batty retirement, and object to him looking at a microscope in his basement while making unsubstantiated claims about cancer. He was investigated. A court ordered that he burn his books and chop up his remaining accumulators. He did.<br /><br />This book is his angry, sustained rant at the critiques and encroachments on his kooky world view. It is rancorous and sad. The book is long howl of a man who has been harmed but still wants to carry on, despite his general misanthropy brought on by being fucked with because he was a strange, alienated loner. It's also kooky much like Reich himself.<br /><br />I am glad to have finally read one of his books. I have been fascinated by Reich since I learned about him from my favourite Kate Bush song, <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IRHA9W-zExQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Cloudbusting</a>. <br /><br /><u>Listen, Little Man!</u> is a later, angry book. Reich seems to want to impart something, but mostly rants that readers are too stupid and narrow minded to listen. His critiques are random, sometimes scoring points. Generally, there is not much beyond Reich sounding aggrieved for not being left alone and for not being recognized as a genius (These were not mutually exclusive in his mind, both based on a cancer cure and a life force that only he could see). At some point, I will read another of his books, probably <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/339384.Character_Analysis" title="Character Analysis by Wilhelm Reich" rel="nofollow noopener">Character Analysis</a>, an earlier book from when he was a Freudian darling. This one was decent, but only read it if you are looking for a scattershot memo on why people generally suck in large groups.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10935739333031320953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_667129350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667129350" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13213337-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353819833p2/13213337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/667129350?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/13213337-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer667129350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2542062071850433587">Under the pretext of showing the Little Man, the Common, Petty Man the error of living trivially, Wilhelm Reich has written an incoherent portrait of a society that persecutes the enlightened, or Great Man in an attempt to defend the legitimacy of his much-criticized "research." He comes from a position of hatred for the contents of the minds of most men and claims to have complete separation from it, then offers the reader the same like an egomaniacal door-to-door salesman. It gets clear as the</span>
  <span id="freeText2542062071850433587" style="display:none">Under the pretext of showing the Little Man, the Common, Petty Man the error of living trivially, Wilhelm Reich has written an incoherent portrait of a society that persecutes the enlightened, or Great Man in an attempt to defend the legitimacy of his much-criticized "research." He comes from a position of hatred for the contents of the minds of most men and claims to have complete separation from it, then offers the reader the same like an egomaniacal door-to-door salesman. It gets clear as the rant (it becomes less and less an essay by the middle) continues that this was never meant to be published and indeed should never have been published without reorganization and clarification. Any apparent insight he has is because he makes grand blanket statements that the reader can apply to the small portion of their lives to which it fits. Eventually the discourse breaks down into criticisms of specific people in his life, including his landlord and one of his employees. His paranoia and disconnect from other people resembles schizophrenia, as does his inability to process reality. Instead of presenting arguments and providing supporting evidence, he attacks those who doubt his claims as afraid of his ideas and suggests that he will one day be worshiped as a genius.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2542062071850433587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13773929020642918107">Wilhelm Reich was evidently quite angry when he wrote this. Plus it wasn't originally intended for publication. This is probably why it's such a rambling, incoheren, ranty mess. It was written just after the end of WW2 and he was obviously reacting to the actions of his fellow Germans during the Third Reich, but still, a little more focus, structure and use of specific examples wouldn't have gone amiss. Instead we get a misanthropic (and at times misogynistic) splenetic outburst, combined with p</span>
  <span id="freeText13773929020642918107" style="display:none">Wilhelm Reich was evidently quite angry when he wrote this. Plus it wasn't originally intended for publication. This is probably why it's such a rambling, incoheren, ranty mess. It was written just after the end of WW2 and he was obviously reacting to the actions of his fellow Germans during the Third Reich, but still, a little more focus, structure and use of specific examples wouldn't have gone amiss. Instead we get a misanthropic (and at times misogynistic) splenetic outburst, combined with plenty of self-promotion and a few token mentions of his "orgone" theories, of which he seems immensely proud, although not enough to bother explaining to us in this context exactly what it is.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2540717251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15115776043138121162">I did not know of Reich until perhaps a couple of weeks ago, when a dear friend suggested it to me saying that she had loved reading it. I can now understand why. In such little space, Reich has talked about human potential and possibility whilst also berating the Little Man and Woman for destroying that very potential. He knocks the Littles down, only in expectation that they will come to think, love, and live for themselves as he asks them to. I do not know how this book fits into Reich's larg</span>
  <span id="freeText15115776043138121162" style="display:none">I did not know of Reich until perhaps a couple of weeks ago, when a dear friend suggested it to me saying that she had loved reading it. I can now understand why. In such little space, Reich has talked about human potential and possibility whilst also berating the Little Man and Woman for destroying that very potential. He knocks the Littles down, only in expectation that they will come to think, love, and live for themselves as he asks them to. I do not know how this book fits into Reich's larger body of work, but by itself it is an easy and enjoyable read, with an important message behind it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15115776043138121162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText10389408537914030624" style="display:none">Too much crap for such a short book.<br /><br />Okay, okay, it had some interesting ideas, like "only you can save yourself" and "you are the one in which your future relies" but I am absolutely sure that there are thousands of books out there that manage to show the same message without all the arrogance and belittlement of others that this author shows through the novel.<br /><br />All the novel can be summed up in this: "Okay you are all little man, which is a synonym for f*cking idiots, and I am the most intelligent person ever, but because of the goodness of my heart I have come to tell you just how stupid you all are and how everything bad that happens in society is your own fault for being such idiots. Oh, and you are welcome"<br /><br />This is an actual quote from the book:<br /><i>I am very deeply afraid of you, Little Man. That has not always been so. These kind of character trait is sadly way too common in people who really are more intelligent than most people, instead of thinking that just because your IQ is a little higher it doesn't mean that the rest of the people are morons, and that was basically what made me skip pages in a 50 pages long book just for it to be over</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer14916816247615495571">People kept praising this book a little too much recently and so I thought it must be a great one to read, especially because I read the Kurdish translation since I figured it would help me get better at reading Kurdish books.<br/><br/>I have to say that I wasn't impressed. I don't think I got a lot of benefit from this one except that it reinforced some ideas I previously had, which is not a bad thing to say about a book by the way. The author presented too many ideas for me to comprehend and I didn't kn</span>
  <span id="freeText14916816247615495571" style="display:none">People kept praising this book a little too much recently and so I thought it must be a great one to read, especially because I read the Kurdish translation since I figured it would help me get better at reading Kurdish books.<br /><br />I have to say that I wasn't impressed. I don't think I got a lot of benefit from this one except that it reinforced some ideas I previously had, which is not a bad thing to say about a book by the way. The author presented too many ideas for me to comprehend and I didn't know where he was trying to get. Though now that I've finished it I can say that I know what it's about.<br /><br />It's a social, psychological, self-help book. The author calls out bullsh*t. He tells you what people are doing wrong, why they do the things they do, and what to do. It's a motivator. It tries to bring out the good and caring person inside you. The author does all of this mainly by commenting on events that have happened to him in a fast pace. The style is confrontational, so it may irritate some people who don't like to be told what to do, at least in the beginning.<br /><br />So "listen, little men!", before reading the book it's better to have an idea about politics of the 20th century and, more importantly, the author: who he is and what he has done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14916816247615495571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_37436824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37436824" />
    <a title="Shawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1697111-shawn"><img alt="Shawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588366811p2/1697111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37436824?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawn" href="/user/show/1697111-shawn">Shawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1697111-shawn?shelf=nf-r-philosophy-oddball-own">nf-r-philosophy-oddball-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37436824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7753262370627619481">Actually, this would probably be a 2.75 or so, ranking-wise. If you know nothing about <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Reich' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wilhelm Reich</a>, this is not the place to start. Even if you do know something about Reich, this book is still an oddity - it contains none of his early work in psychiatry (done with Freud), and only contains his later, more controversial and "fringier" ideas (that precursored the sexual revolution) as background. This book is not a "sketch it out for the layman" instruction manual, either, despite its deceptive</span>
  <span id="freeText7753262370627619481" style="display:none">Actually, this would probably be a 2.75 or so, ranking-wise. If you know nothing about <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Reich" rel="nofollow noopener">Wilhelm Reich</a>, this is not the place to start. Even if you do know something about Reich, this book is still an oddity - it contains none of his early work in psychiatry (done with Freud), and only contains his later, more controversial and "fringier" ideas (that precursored the sexual revolution) as background. This book is not a "sketch it out for the layman" instruction manual, either, despite its deceptive/simplistic packaging. What LISTEN, LITTLE MAN! is, is partially a rant, partially a screed, and partially a heartfelt cry from a smart man who really, honestly believed he was doing right, had been wronged by many, and who may also have been teetering on the edge of mental problems.<br /><br />I consider myself a rationalist, but I understand the imaginative, visionary power of irrational thought and a balance between the two has guided me happily, if not easily, through life. And also, thanks to early exposure to the writings of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/160301.Charles_Fort" title="Charles Fort" rel="nofollow noopener">Charles Fort</a> (grandfather to the concept of paranormal phenomena and arch-cynic/satirist/iconoloclast, an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7805.H_L__Mencken" title="H.L. Mencken" rel="nofollow noopener">H.L. Mencken</a> of the weird who tilted at turn-of-the-century science's windmills), I learned to distrust any claims of absolute knowledge. I find some of Reich's work, especially his early theories of body armoring (the root of Reichian theory), to be interesting and potentially valid. His later work - research that, in an attempt to prove his theories, moved out of psychiatry into theoretical physics/biology with the supposed discovery of orgone and the bion - certainly seems unlikely and scientifically unsupportable, but if treated conceptually instead of rationally, it has a visionary/artistic/poetic quality I can respect, even if I don't believe in it. Like a lot of people, I first heard of Reich through the works of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2918.Robert_Anton_Wilson" title="Robert Anton Wilson" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Anton Wilson</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5025.William_S__Burroughs" title="William S. Burroughs" rel="nofollow noopener">William S. Burroughs</a>, Reich having been a bit of an outlaw hero to the Beats, 60s Counterculturals and 70s New-Agers and Occultists (Wilson, specifically, writes very movingly on Reich's demonization by the U.S. Government and the burning of his books). Now, some may see in Reich either a charlatan (selling cancer cures to unsuspecting rubes like thousands of other scam artists that the Government should be protecting the populace from) or a quack (in the sense that he honestly believed what he was espousing, but it was still unproven and potentially dangerous) - and I can't honestly say that I have an opinion one way or the other, but my reading of writings by Reich himself gives me the feeling he truly believed his theories. One of those writings is LISTEN, LITTLE MAN!<br /><br />Which is all a long and involved way of getting to the point - this book is basically Reich defending himself against his real and perceived enemies and attempting to explain to his detractors how all of their beliefs about him arise from their own complexes.<br /><br />At times it is moving and eloquent - reading between the lines, you can see a smart, observant, deeply emotional man who grew up during/lived through some of the most tumultuous and terrible times in European and World history: two World Wars, the Holocaust, the rise of Capitalism and Communism, the Stalinist purges and assorted massacres, the Atom Bomb. He believes in psychiatry and analysis as the new tools to save mankind from itself, to stop it from repeating the hideous acts already perpetrated by man against man, even as these same acts were escalating in horrible ways. He finds himself accepted and then rejected as he refuses to comply to any one political movement; mocked, reviled and slandered, chased throughout Europe, accepted in the U.S. and then attacked again. As his theories all revolve around sex, he is naively unprepared for the intensity of the public's reaction to gossip and misinformation, and their automatic assumption that anything involving sex must be dirty, lewd and pornographic. He works endlessly to develop his ideas and then prove them, all for the benefit of people who despise and mistrust him.<br /><br />Unfortunately, at times (perhaps, more often) LISTEN, LITTLE MAN! is also paranoid and hectoring, defensive and arrogant. At times, Reich's anectodal recitation of the sins against him, all perpetrated by different individuals but all addressed to the titular "little man", sounds nothing but bitter - nursed wounds that have festered in the heart of a man who is now unloading his bile on the fools who will not realize he is working to save them. At times a messiah/martyr complex can be seen building behind the words, believed by a man who wants desperately to save everyone from their worst selves through the tools of love and orgasms, and a man who absolutely believes that he completely understands why people do the awful things they do, and how they could stop doing them if only they would... "listen, little man!" <br /><br />And so, this is an interesting document. Not the first, or best, thing by Wilhelm Reich to be read - a text that cannot support itself, but provides fascinating glimspes at the thoughts of a complicated, conflicted man. And not all of it is just an object lesson in the dangers of fringe thinking, self-confidence and public opprobrium. Some gems of Reichian thought shine through the paranoia and didactic rhetoric, bright gleamings that sketch the borders of Reich's vision, his ability to clearly see some, if not all, of the problems we face. Quotes will follow. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7753262370627619481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3169992841?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2020</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1555152611388814594">" قبل أن تفكروا بالتخلص من حاكم مستبد، تخلصوا مما يستبد بكم من عادات سيئة وتقاليد سوداء. " ميخائيل نعيمة<br/>What life consists of is the dimensional matrix of events floating around the so-called “reality, and how the protagonists “us,” who are placed involuntarily inside this matrix manage to deal with these realities. <br/>Well, even with this illusionary nature, we have a minor agency to control our virtual existence, and it's best if we practiced this agency upon ourselves before others.<br/> That’s someh</span>
  <span id="freeText1555152611388814594" style="display:none">" قبل أن تفكروا بالتخلص من حاكم مستبد، تخلصوا مما يستبد بكم من عادات سيئة وتقاليد سوداء. " ميخائيل نعيمة<br />What life consists of is the dimensional matrix of events floating around the so-called “reality, and how the protagonists “us,” who are placed involuntarily inside this matrix manage to deal with these realities. <br />Well, even with this illusionary nature, we have a minor agency to control our virtual existence, and it's best if we practiced this agency upon ourselves before others.<br /> That’s somehow linked to our current state and the misunderstanding of revolutionary decisions. <br />I decided to stay out of the ongoing argument by most people, which reflects only one side of the multi-sided equation. ( this particular equation happens to have more than two sides, becz it’s no longer algebra that we’re discussing here. I know that it’s already too late but this book has paved the way for this review.. <br /> Anyhow, revolutions across history haven’t always succeeded in obtaining social and political reforms. Including the revolutions in Syria, Yemen, Egypt, and Libya. <br />Reasons included the emotional drives behind the revolution, the unorganized procedure, which combines the essence of the starting point of the action with the goal of the revolution itself, and the emphasis on politics rather than the whole picture of the chaotic reality that’s experienced by individuals. <br />I’m NOT saying that revolutions couldn’t or didn’t make any change, but the root of the uprisings has always been reactionary in nature and focusing only on political realities. This is exclusively true for Iraq, the Middle East, Asia, and Africa. (in the modern historical sense)<br /><br />I wasn’t planning to write anything about the “so-called October demonstration” until i started reading this book. <br />I was also witnessing the nature of MOST ppl, who are standing against ( again ) “the so-called” corrupt system.<br /> I don’t actually support the government.. I’m not against the protesters either.<br /> I simply think that everyone has the right to express their freedom the way they feel “comfortable with. <br />I know that in some occasions, one can’t stay neutral and has to take a stand, but that’s only when one is completely convinced about the drives and the outcomes behind the bias position they’re following. <br />Freedom has never been only about revolutions. <br />This freedom of choice and action, though limited, should be exercised deliberately. <br />The whole concept of belonging and what comes after such as “patriotism is an artificial creation of who we should be, ( rather who we want to be.) <br />Turning back to the victimization image that most ppl have been eagerly trying to draw throughout their lives, political instability has never been the cause of one side over the other. <br />If we, for example, were born and found ourselves believing in a certain or multiple gods, and then we were raised to follow the teachings of a particular belief, but it turned out eventually that we’ve been deceived somehow.. then it’s our fault from the first place, not gods or the religious image that others have created to pass it to us. <br />Accordingly, by not choosing our own path, we ended up following the footsteps of our inherited identity. The same principle here applies to the current political status in iraq.. <br />ppl have not only followed the stereotypical image imposed by the political and social systems, they have also chosen their representatives. <br />They have enforced the laws upon themselves. They have allowed corruption to be passed under the name of religious and tribal values. <br />They have lived and learned to adapt to this unbalanced social landscape. <br />Another point worth mentioning is that some ppl are starting to link awareness with the blurred political and national identity .. <br />Some are also attacking, rather than trying to understand, the true nature of difference. <br />Those ppl are still fighting over who loves their country more, who can protest longer, who can deliver the brightest speeches about human rights and patriotism, who can repeatedly post revolutionary essays or pictures on their social media page to show their support, who can publish the bestselling book to show their support ( not gonna mention those who were killed, becz obviously, they’re not bragging about their death.) <br />Most of the ppl are also criticizing those who are not by their side. Some of them even attack whoever has a different insight. It’s like a competition, either you join this gigantic nationalistic bubble or you’re labeled as a traitor.<br /><br />But wait, before calling for ur basic rights.. let’s list some of the mutual characteristics that MOST of you guys ( protesters) share with the corrupt structure you’re rising against..<br /><br />Who is still praising saddam until this very moment, and regard him as a charismatic leader by comparing our current state with the so-called “glorious” one under his leadership?! <br /><br />Who represents “ abul-kareem qasim” as the most perfect iraqi president without pointing out to the fact that he’s a murder after all, and almost all political figures at some point or another are murders. Thus, they shouldn’t be glorified?! <br /><br />Who praises political and religious figures publicly to the point where some ppl try to touch those “ holy” subjects just to be blessed by their halo?! <br /><br />Who refuses to hire anyone in the public or the private sector unless they have political or social patronage?! <br /><br />Who listens repeatedly to the religious speeches delivered by the ‘so-called’ religious leaders, who have been intervening in politics and brainwashing ppl for the past 16 years?! (and maybe more!<br /><br />Who views difference as a kind of a disease and attacks whoever disagrees with their basic principles or beliefs?! <br /><br />Who believes that kurds should be under the mercy of the arab regime and kurdish independence is just another dream that not only can’t be achieved but it’s constantly fought against?! <br /><br />Who argues that yazidis deserve what they have been through and should be exterminated because they worship satan?! <br /><br />Who thinks that Christians, Shabaks, and Mandaeans are only a minority in iraq. That’s why they’re cast out of cultural, political and social activities?! <br /><br />Who participates in every election to select the candidates according to their own interests ( mostly religious)?! <br /><br />Who engages in behaviors including giving out bribes or receiving them just to get their business done?! <br /><br />Who attends schools or universities ( most of the teachers and professors) just to get paid without giving a damn about the whole fucked up curriculums or the teaching process?! (okay, this might be universal) <br /><br />Who follows the idiotic figures on social media and let them control ur look, ideas, and values?<br /><br />Who blackmails anyone who comes into their mind ( as a way to take revenge or make fun of someone) and when it gets worse” when the victim is harmed, no legal or social justice is taken place, (not only sexual abuse) ?! <br /><br />Who travels to neighboring countries just to have sex while they’re already married and having a shitty family?! ( While banning prostitution)! <br /><br />Who talks about ethics and value in public while committing the most horrific actions when no one is watching?! <br /><br />Who smiles at your face while talking about you behind ur back, and that’s when u hear things that can never be found even in fiction books?!<br /><br />Who throws away garbage in the streets or throw it out of the car as an easy way to get rid of their own fucking shit?! But when abroad, adopts the manners and etiquette of the foreign culture.. ?!<br /><br />Who highlights medicine and other relatable fields as the “most prestigious” domains in the post-high school phase, and drives their children to study within the scope of this arena just to acquire more money and to acquire a place in the social ladder?! <br /><br />Who discourages any kind of creativity in art, sports, music, or literature, and consider the whole idea of creativity as a waste of time?! <br /><br />Who sets the rules for female/ male identity and assigns certain characteristics to each gender, who standardizes gender roles and whoever goes against them, then he/she must be mental/ defective person?! <br /><br />Who ignores the acts of the children or even the adults who use violence against animals without having the slightest regret of their behavior?! <br /><br />Who judges others by their appearance and labels them according to their social status?! <br /><br />Who dishonor women who are raped and refuse the act of abortion?! Who marries raped women off to their rapists?? <br /><br />Who teaches children that males should take every advantage coming into their way and should never hesitate in doing anything that pleases them including raping children or women if they were aroused suddenly?! Plus, no social, prior to “legal, action is taken against minor marriages or even incest crimes! <br /><br />Who insults divorced women/ widows/ single women and comes up with the most imaginative rumors of them ?! <br />Who gives speeches about women’s chastity and the fact that every woman should end up living under a cold ceiling surrounded by rusty walls just to be fucked and produce more pathetic creatures?! Who enforces the laws of marriage and the need to “ catch the train before it’s too late? The need to prove the latest scientific discovery to society ( that humans are actually mammals. Shh! That’s just between us!) / so society needs to see the proof “ the doomed child” , the fact that females can get pregnant and carry a foetus inside their wombs, while males can make all the magic come true with the power of their sperms..!<br /><br />Who perceives men who can express their feelings or care and respect other humans or animals.. those who refuse any acts of violence as weak or dysfunctional males?! <br /><br />Who excludes the fact that men can be sensitive and whoever doesn’t follow the masculine guideline, then he must be a homosexual?! Or mentally unstable ?! Or the opposite to women with no stereotypical feminine features attached.. <br />who regards the term homosexual / transgender/ bisexual ..etc ( everything related to sexual “ private/personal” identity) as a curse?! <br />Who considers men and women who don’t end up being<br />married as some kind of lousy individuals?! <br />Who measures others' morality by their sexuality?! <br /><br /><br />Who has invented the whole structure of cursing language and the feminization/ masculinization of every filthy concept?! <br /><br />Who claims that males who are raped or are sexually, mentally, physically or verbally abused don’t even exist and it’s only a feminine matter? <br /><br />Who puts pressure on male-female relationships and prohibits any kind of voluntary mutual tendencies towards making a bond, (not necessarily sexual) unless this bond is labeled legally and religiously ?! <br /><br />Who measures the value of the bride by her dowry and the bride (the thing), who is bought by the highest price, then she’s the most valuable person?! <br /><br />Who argues that men should hold the financial responsibility of their family and women shouldn’t have the slightest contribution to their family?! Becz they’re queens, after all!! <br /><br />Who stigmatizes ppl who are open about their mental health?! Who avoids talking about mental issues and perceives mental institutions as a kind of black secretive and an untouchable zone?! <br /><br />Who teaches children that bullying is just another “ daily activity” ?! <br /><br />Who promotes the fact that ppl can do no matter what they want to do as long as they are believers who pray and ask for god’s forgiveness?! <br /><br />Who sets the rules of the social norms and injects them directly into the political system?! <br /><br />The list goes on and on... ( and btw, some points don’t only apply to the “ Iraqi community,” some are universal matters.. So, this excessive corruption is not exclusively true for iraq! <br />Indeed, Every single society is dealing with the same issues! Or even more. <br />What’s different here is that we blame only governments for what we are.. we blame others so we can feel better about ourselves. <br />It’s not only politics, it’s never been.. the accumulation of these deep-rooted values and social construction are the most powerful influence on who we are and what we’ve become. <br />It’s us! It’s always been us! <br /><br />I’m not writing this as a knowledgeable person, in a way or another, I’m also included here. <br />It's just a response for those who think that a revolution is defined as the ultimate stand taken by a group of angry ppl, who are sick and tired of their oppressive systems.<br />Well, let me tell you sth ( you who think that you’re oppressed), you’ve had many chances to change who you are, to change the essence of ur identity, to acknowledge that what you’ve been taught and raised upon is just another kind of slavery, but you never took these chances. <br />Even now, you’re still attacking those who are against you. You’ve never changed. <br />Most of you never will. <br />Iraq or any other shitty country doesn’t need political reforms. Constitutions aren’t thrown out of the sky. Ppl participate in the creation of politics.<br />Political reforms including the democratic image sponsored by some are just a shallow image of our corrupted selves. <br /><br />Ppl need to confront who they are before confronting their governments. <br />Ppl need to let those who don’t share the same opinions alone. <br />Ppl need to discuss their differences, not attack them. <br />This can be seen by some as an idealistic representation of a utopian state since conflicts are essentially inevitable and peace is just another fantasy. <br />I agree with that, but i also think that if we want to express who we truly are, if we want to gain a slice of the so-called “freedom, then we’ll have to learn how to respect diversity. <br />We’ll have to learn how to think before we say anything. <br />This idea of the imposed collective identity ( advertised in the demonstration) will reproduce another slavery. <br />We have to let each person fight or express themselves in their way. <br />I used to admire most of the revolutionary figures (especially in the political and economic spheres) including Lenin, Marx, Gandhi, Guevara, Castro.. <br />But then I’d realized that it was all a huge propaganda to sell some repetitive ideas in the name of freedom. I’m not saying that they’re a bunch of jerks, who have no contribution wtsoever to their nations. They’re just ordinary people, who hadn’t introduced anything different from their preceding regimes. (continued on fb)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4789721570254333285">A small reflection, from a misunderstood man of his time. <br/>Although I recognize he might have been really upset with society, while he was writing this short conversation with the little man ( and woman!), and sometimes he thinks he has all the answers ( but of course he is only a human being and doesn't know everything, and I do have some critics to this book), but the thing is that he really shows us our incapability of being who we truly are, of demonstrating our opinions ( as we are always lo</span>
  <span id="freeText4789721570254333285" style="display:none">A small reflection, from a misunderstood man of his time. <br />Although I recognize he might have been really upset with society, while he was writing this short conversation with the little man ( and woman!), and sometimes he thinks he has all the answers ( but of course he is only a human being and doesn't know everything, and I do have some critics to this book), but the thing is that he really shows us our incapability of being who we truly are, of demonstrating our opinions ( as we are always looking for some sort of "savior" to our lives, our countries, etc)~ Our inability to know who we are in this world of ours. He didn't belong to this or that political side, to this or that religion, to this or that country . With him, slogans only serve to make us more slaves than we already are... Slogans restrain our capability of thinking differently, cause if we belong to a certain political side, for example, even if we think in a different way of our " side" or we want to criticize something wrong that our political side did, we will think twice , before having courage to show our voice. The thing that I most liked during my reading was that he saw the world as one, he encouraged people to do their work well, to love and by extension, have sex with the ones they love and love them back, and live their lives in peace, knowing how to respect and be respected. As it was written in a post-war context and seeing that this book applies to our society from today, to me, in the end, it sounded like an Utopia.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8308682843009416696">“You differ from a great man in only one respect: the great man was once a very little man, but he developed one important quality: he recognized the smallness and narrowness of his thoughts and actions. Under the pressure of some task that meant a great deal to him, he learned to see how his smallness, his pettiness endangered his happiness. In other words, a great man knows when and in what way he is a little man. A little man does not know he is little and is afraid to know. He hides his pett</span>
  <span id="freeText8308682843009416696" style="display:none">“You differ from a great man in only one respect: the great man was once a very little man, but he developed one important quality: he recognized the smallness and narrowness of his thoughts and actions. Under the pressure of some task that meant a great deal to him, he learned to see how his smallness, his pettiness endangered his happiness. In other words, a great man knows when and in what way he is a little man. A little man does not know he is little and is afraid to know. He hides his pettiness and narrowness behind illusions of strength and greatness, someone else's strength and greatness. He's proud of his great generals but not of himself. He admires an idea he has not had, not one he has had. The less he understands something, the more firmly he believes in it. And the better he understands an idea, the less he believes in it.”<br />― Wilhelm Reich, Listen, Little Man! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8308682843009416696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8226422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8077999964099556777">This book is good, in that it puts stupidity in its place. It provides a good view of how our selves are the greatest obstructions to our own progress and well-being. It points out the smallness that hides in all of us, with the hope that by being aware of it, we might be able to transcend it. <br/>I agree with Reich that his research should not be judged on a moral reactive basis, but with sound reasoning. Unfortunately, I'm not sure how much sound reasoning has ever been invested into Reichian ther</span>
  <span id="freeText8077999964099556777" style="display:none">This book is good, in that it puts stupidity in its place. It provides a good view of how our selves are the greatest obstructions to our own progress and well-being. It points out the smallness that hides in all of us, with the hope that by being aware of it, we might be able to transcend it. <br />I agree with Reich that his research should not be judged on a moral reactive basis, but with sound reasoning. Unfortunately, I'm not sure how much sound reasoning has ever been invested into Reichian therapy and Orgone. Reich is a bit egotistical when he claims that he will be revered in the future as the one who showed how to cure all illnesses, cancer in particular. <br />I'm not saying Orgone isn't real, just that it should be investigated, and not accepted to be real just because Reich is your hero. <br />The mood of the book is somewhat distractingly dated, in that much focus is directed towards the communist/capitalist dialectic. This was much more prominent during the time the book was written. But the ideas still apply to modern times, only slightly modified. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8077999964099556777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2734782218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2734782218" />
    <a title="Elliot Ratzman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1999603-elliot-ratzman"><img alt="Elliot Ratzman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308703863p2/1999603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2734782218?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elliot Ratzman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elliot Ratzman" href="/user/show/1999603-elliot-ratzman">Elliot Ratzman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734782218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1718740608682619350">“I have discovered the laws of living energy…your cosmic essence.” Written in the mid-40s, this is one long stream of narcissistic rant by Reich, complemented with cartoony illustrations by William Steig (creator of Shrek!) that undermine the seriousness (or seriously deluded) tone of Reich’s legal situation. Paranoid and resentful, he sees the “little man” out to get him in particular, and the genius/great man in general. By this time he was living in Maine, claiming to have discovered the cure</span>
  <span id="freeText1718740608682619350" style="display:none">“I have discovered the laws of living energy…your cosmic essence.” Written in the mid-40s, this is one long stream of narcissistic rant by Reich, complemented with cartoony illustrations by William Steig (creator of Shrek!) that undermine the seriousness (or seriously deluded) tone of Reich’s legal situation. Paranoid and resentful, he sees the “little man” out to get him in particular, and the genius/great man in general. By this time he was living in Maine, claiming to have discovered the cure for cancer, the secrets of the universal energy, and, from the book, apparently advocating for open sexuality by youths and adolescents. Like a comic book villain, he decries the “distract attorneys and judges” that hound him. Whoops! There are racist and sexist passages that don’t hold up to today’s standards, and he seems to collapse complex phenomena into failures of nerve, the refusal of the little man to “be himself” or something vague, intermixed with his own confidence in his own genius.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1718740608682619350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('enc2Sa2hbx9nHb5mjraaZj9JxNdiJrzzoTWmbqTcrKhysSxBzkukE+TNHQ6JovIOm2hUVRwGn7doqVnvRJheJQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+kEImi1jdLWWFjd7u8x5SQiAXPM7dzhvVzYeLWtnGmXyhxKSTom/uRXGlBO82BEhrKHMcUVXGyuequGsiyPo6A==')})
  }

A la evidente nunca innecesaria reflexión sobre el lugar del poder en la sociedad actual -que también sería una reflexión sobre la violencia establecida como realidad social y económica-, el Pessoa de &quot;El banquero anarquista&quot; remite también al albedrío de los individuos. Cuestiona el poder vertical, a la par que acepta su existencia como algo de lo que vale la pena escapar -lo cual sólo puede acontecer, según el sofista, con sus propias armas y herramientas. Al tocar el tema de la riqueza en tanto meta de nuestra sociedad advierte, no sin cruenta paradoja, que en la acumulación de riquezas reside cuando menos la ilusión de una salida individual a la presión social. Este relato-diálogo revela, pleno de ironía -de decepción asimilada-, aun dentro de los más elevados ideales tópicos subyacentes, la inquietante presencia de la contradicción como elemento       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/118694.Wilhelm_Reich">About Wilhelm Reich</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/118694.Wilhelm_Reich"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1521072495p3/118694.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/118694.Wilhelm_Reich">Wilhelm Reich
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
465
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13940542154183866449">Jewish Austrian-American psychiatrist and psychoanalyst.<br/><br/>Reich was a respected analyst for much of his life, focusing on character structure, rather than on individual neurotic symptoms. He promoted adolescent sexuality, the availability of contraceptives and abortion, and the importance for women of economic independence. Synthesizing material from psychoanalysis, cultural anthropology, economics,</span>
  <span id="freeText13940542154183866449" style="display:none">Jewish Austrian-American psychiatrist and psychoanalyst.<br /><br />Reich was a respected analyst for much of his life, focusing on character structure, rather than on individual neurotic symptoms. He promoted adolescent sexuality, the availability of contraceptives and abortion, and the importance for women of economic independence. Synthesizing material from psychoanalysis, cultural anthropology, economics, sociology, and ethics, his work influenced writers such as Alexander Lowen, Fritz Perls, Paul Goodman, Saul Bellow, Norman Mailer, A. S. Neill, and William Burroughs.<br /><br />He was also a controversial figure, who came to be viewed by the psychoanalytic establishment as having gone astray or as having succumbed to mental illness. His work on the link between human sexuality and neuroses emphasized "orgastic potency" as the foremost criterion for psycho-physical health. He said he had discovered a form of energy, which he called "orgone," that permeated the atmosphere and all living matter, and he built "orgone accumulators," which his patients sat inside to harness the energy for its reputed health benefits. It was this work, in particular, that cemented the rift between Reich and the psychoanalytic establishment.<br /><br />Reich, of Jewish descent and a communist, was living in Germany when Adolf Hitler came to power. He fled to Scandinavia in 1933 and subsequently to the United States in 1939. In 1947, following a series of critical articles about orgone and his political views in <i>The New Republic</i> and <i>Harper's</i>, the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) began an investigation into his claims, winning an injunction against the interstate sale of orgone accumulators. Charged with contempt of court for violating the injunction, Reich conducted his own defense, which involved sending the judge all his books to read, and arguing that a court was no place to decide matters of science. He was sentenced to two years in prison, and in August 1956, several tons of his publications were burned by the FDA. He died of heart failure in jail just over a year later, days before he was due to apply for parole.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13940542154183866449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/414183-rede-an-den-kleinen-mann">Quotes from Listen, Little Man!</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;You differ from a great man in only one respect: the great man was once a very little man, but he developed one important quality: he recognized the smallness and narrowness of his thoughts and actions. Under the pressure of some task that meant a great deal to him, he learned to see how his smallness, his pettiness endangered his happiness. In other words, a great man knows when and in what way he is a little man. A little man does not know he is little and is afraid to know. He hides his pettiness and narrowness behind illusions of strength and greatness, someone else's strength and greatness. He's proud of his great generals but not of himself. He admires an idea he has not had, not one he has had. The less he understands something, the more firmly he believes in it. And the better he understands an idea, the less he believes in it.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/272480-you-differ-from-a-great-man-in-only-one-respect">214 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;You'll have a good, secure life when being alive means more to you than security, love more than money, your freedom more than public or partisan opinion, when the mood of Beethoven's or Bach's music becomes the mood of your whole life … when your thinking is in harmony, and no longer in conflict, with your feelings … when you let yourself be guided by the thoughts of great sages and no longer by the crimes of great warriors … when you pay the men and women who teach your children better than the politicians; when truths inspire you and empty formulas repel you; when you communicate with your fellow workers in foreign countries directly, and no longer through diplomats...&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/272512-you-ll-have-a-good-secure-life-when-being-alive-means">157 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/414183-rede-an-den-kleinen-mann">More quotes&hellip;</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
